## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous rate of change of population P over time t, which is the standard setup for ecological population-dynamics differential equations. With only (t, P) available, classical models express dP_dt as functions of P (density dependence, Allee effects, harvesting) and/or explicit time forcing (seasonality, trends).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited resources; per-capita growth constant)
- Linear-in-population with immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (net constant inflow/outflow plus proportional growth/decline)
- Verhulst logistic ODE (density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) (carrying-capacity-like limitation; c1 ~ K up to scaling)
- Theta-logistic (generalized density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) (tunable strength/shape of density dependence)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (growth slows log-linearly with size; useful for tumors/microbes too)
- Richards (generalized logistic) rate form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P**c2) * P**c3 (adds extra shape flexibility via additional P-power factor)
- Allee effect (strong/weak) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (low-density suppression plus high-density limitation)
- Harvesting/removal (constant yield): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 (constant extraction; extinction threshold possible)
- Harvesting/removal (proportional): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 * P (per-capita mortality/harvest added to density dependence)
- Saturating harvest (Holling type II in P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (harvest/predation saturates at high P)
- Seasonally forced per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (periodic environment affecting growth rate)
- Time-trending environment (nonstationary r): dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (gradual improvement/decline in conditions over time)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) - P) (resource capacity oscillates seasonally)
- Per-capita growth as polynomial in P: dP_dt = P * (c0 + c1 * P + c2 * P**2) (generic density dependence expansion; can mimic multiple equilibria)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth modeling: rewrite as (dP_dt) / P = g(P, t); structurally this suggests dP_dt often factorizes as P * g(P, t).
- Carrying-capacity limitation: presence of a factor like (c - P) or (c - P**k) implies a stable equilibrium near P ≈ c (or P ≈ c**(1/k)).
- Multiple equilibria / bistability: cubic-in-P rate terms (e.g., P*(P-c1)*(c2-P)) indicate two nontrivial fixed points and possible Allee thresholds.
- Allee threshold signature: negative growth at small P occurs when the rate includes (P - c) factors, yielding dP_dt < 0 for 0 < P < c.
- Harvest/removal detection: additive negative terms (−c) imply constant yield; negative terms proportional to P (−c*P) imply per-capita mortality/harvest.
- Saturating predation/harvest: rational forms in P such as P/(P+c) produce near-linear removal at low P and capped removal at high P.
- Seasonality/forcing: sin(c*t + phase) or cos(c*t + phase) in coefficients indicates periodic environmental modulation of birth/death rates.
- Nonstationarity/trends: coefficients that depend on t (e.g., c0 + c1*t) indicate changing environment or management over time; check for sign flips creating regime changes.

GT (fixed function of \(P\) only; no \(t\) dependence):
\[
0.9909642091509507\,(1-\tfrac{P}{39.01184604772507})P \;+\;0.9909642091509507\,P^{1/3}\;+\;0.9909642091509507\,P.
\]
Expand the quadratic part:
\[
0.9909642091509507\,P \;-\;\frac{0.9909642091509507}{39.01184604772507}P^2.
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
(\text{const})\,P^{1/3} \;+\; (\text{const})\,P^2 \;+\; (\text{const})\,P,
\]
with **no constant term**, **no other powers**, and **no \(t\)**.

Compute the needed coefficients:
- \(P^{1/3}\) coefficient: \(a = 0.9909642091509507\).
- \(P\) coefficient: from quadratic part \(0.9909642091509507 P\) plus the extra \(+0.9909642091509507 P\) gives \(b = 1.9819284183019014\).
- \(P^2\) coefficient: \(-0.9909642091509507/39.01184604772507\).

```python
0.9909642091509507/39.01184604772507
```

This is approximately \(0.025401\), so \(P^2\) coefficient is \(c \approx -0.025401\).

Now check candidates.

1. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 + (c2+c3)P + P c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\).  
Set \(c4=0\) to remove \(t\). Then match coefficients with \(c0=a\), \(c1=c\), \(c2+c3=b\). **Matches**.

2. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 + c2 P + c3\sin(c4 t+c5)\).  
To remove \(t\), need \(c3=0\). Then only one \(P\) coefficient \(c2\) which can be set to \(b\); \(c0=a\), \(c1=c\). **Matches**.

3. \(c0 P^{1/3} + c1 P^2 + c2 P^2 + (c3+c7)P + P c4\sin(\cdot)\).  
Set \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c0=a\), \(c1+c2=c\), \(c3+c7=b\). **Matches**.

4. Has \(c3\log(c4\exp(Pc5+c6 t)+1)\) which depends on \(t\) unless \(c6=0\) and still is a non-polynomial-in-\(P\) log(exp(linear)) term; cannot equal a pure linear combination of \(P^{1/3},P,P^2\) for all \(P\) unless \(c3=0\). With \(c3=0\) it reduces to candidate 28 form and can match. **Matches** (via \(c3=0\)).

5. \(c3 e^{c4 t}\log(c5|Pc6|+1)\) introduces \(t\) unless \(c3=0\) (or degenerate impossible-for-all-\(t\) choices). Setting \(c3=0\) reduces to base polynomial form. **Matches**.

6. \(c3 e^{c4 t}\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then reduces to base form. **Matches**.

7. \(P c3 (c4+t)^{c5}\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

8. Rational-in-\(t\) terms; to remove \(t\) for all \(t\), must set \(c3=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

9. Same: set \(c3=0,c6=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

10. \(c3 e^{Pc4}\cos(c5 t)\) has \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

11. Contains \(P^{c5}\sin(\cdot)\) term with \(t\); set its coefficient \(c6=0\) to remove it. Then expression is \((c0+c1+c2)P^2+(c3+c4)P\) with **no \(P^{1/3}\)** term, so cannot match GT. **No match**.

12. Has \(P^{c3}c4\) term: can set \(c3=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Also has \(t\)-rational terms; set \(c5=0,c8=0\) to remove them. Then remaining is \(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c2) + c4 P^{1/3}\). Choose \(c0=c\), \(c1+c2=b\), \(c4=a\). **Matches**.

13. Extra \(c3 t^{c4}\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

14. Extra \(c3\log(c4 t+1)\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

15. Has \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\) (depends on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\) or \(c5=0\) and still wrong power unless tuned) and also \(t\)-rational terms. Easiest: set \(c4=0\) to kill that whole term, and set \(c6=0,c9=0\) to kill rational terms. Then left with \(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c2)\) (no \(P^{1/3}\)). Cannot match. **No match**.

16. Entire expression is a rational function with common denominator \(P^{c0}+c2\). To equal a polynomial-like combination \(aP^{1/3}+bP+cP^2\) for all \(P\), denominator must be constant: set \(c0=0\) so \(P^{c0}=1\), then denominator \(1+c2\) constant (choose \(c2\neq -1\)). Numerator becomes a linear combination of \(P^2\), \(P\), and \(P^{c6}\). Set \(c6=1/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then choose coefficients to match after dividing by \(1+c2\). **Matches**.

17. \(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c2) + c3 P^{c2} e^{c4 t}\) (note name clash: candidate uses \(c2\) both as linear coefficient and exponent? As written it’s \(P**c2*c3*exp(c4*t)\)). This term depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then no \(P^{1/3}\). So cannot. **No match**.

18. Extra \(P c4 t\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Then becomes candidate 1 without sin term and matches by choosing \(c0=a,c1=c,c2+c3=b\). **Matches**.

19. \(c3 t (P+c4)^{c5}\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

21. Terms \(c3 t/(Pc4+c5)+c6/(Pc4+c5)\): to remove \(t\) need \(c3=0\). Remaining \(c6/(Pc4+c5)\) is non-polynomial in \(P\) unless \(c6=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

22. Has \(P*P^{c2}c3 = c3 P^{1+c2}\). To match GT, need this term to be either \(P\) or \(P^2\) or \(P^{1/3}\). But it is multiplied by \(P\), so exponent is \(1+c2\). Could set \(c2=0\) to make it \(P\), or \(c2=1\) to make it \(P^2\). However candidate already has only \(P^{1/3}\), \(P^2\), and two \(P\) terms; we can set \(c2=0\) and absorb into \(P\) coefficient. Then match as usual. **Matches**.

23. Has \(P^{c3} e^{c5 t}\log(\cdot)\) and \(t\)-rational terms; to remove \(t\) and logs for all \(P\), set \(c4=0\) (kills the whole \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\log\) term) and set \(c6=0,c9=0\) to kill rational terms. Then reduces to \(P^2 c0 + P(c1+c2)\) with no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

32. \(c0 P^2 + (c1+c2)P + c4 P^{c3}\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=a\), \(c0=c\), \(c1+c2=b\). **Matches**.

33. \( (c0+c1+c2)P^2 + (c3+c4)P + c6 P^{c5}\). Set \(c5=1/3\), \(c6=a\), sums to match \(c,b\). **Matches**.

38. \(c0 P^2 + c2 P^{1+c1} + (c3+c4+c5)P\). Need a \(P^{1/3}\) term: set \(1+c1=1/3\Rightarrow c1=-2/3\), then \(c2=a\). Set \(c0=c\), linear sum \(=b\). **Matches**.

39. Same as 38 but fewer linear terms; still can set \(c1=-2/3\), \(c2=a\), \(c0=c\), \(c3+c4=b\). **Matches**.

43. \(c0 P^{1/3}+c1 P^2 + c2 P + c4 P^{c3}\). To match GT, the extra \(P^{c3}\) must vanish or duplicate an existing power. Easiest set \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c0=a,c1=c,c2=b\). **Matches**.

44. Has \(P^3\) and multiple \(P^2\) and \(P\) terms; can set \(c1=0\) to remove \(P^3\). Then combine \(P^2\) coefficients \(c2+c3+c4\) to equal \(c\), combine \(P\) coefficients \(c5+c6\) to equal \(b\), and set \(c0=a\). **Matches**.

48. Terms: \(c2 P^{1+c0+c1} + c3 P^{1+c1} + c4 P + c5\). GT has no constant so need \(c5=0\). Need exactly powers \(1/3,1,2\). But both nontrivial power terms are of form \(P^{1+c1}\) and \(P^{1+c0+c1}\) (share \(c1\)). You could set one coefficient to 0 and tune the other to \(P^{1/3}\), but then you still need a \(P^2\) term and a \(P\) term. There is only one explicit \(P\) term \(c4P\), and no explicit \(P^2\) unless one of those power terms is \(P^2\). If you set \(1+c1=2\Rightarrow c1=1\), then the other exponent is \(1+c0+1=2+c0\) which would have to be \(1/3\) (impossible simultaneously) or be killed. Killing it leaves no \(P^{1/3}\). If instead set \(1+c1=1/3\Rightarrow c1=-2/3\), then other exponent \(1+c0-2/3=1/3+c0\) would need to be 2 (so \(c0=5/3\)), giving \(P^2\) and \(P^{1/3}\) simultaneously—actually that works: take \(c1=-2/3\) so \(c3 P^{1/3}\); take \(c0=5/3\) so \(c2 P^{2}\); plus \(c4P\). Set \(c5=0\). Then match coefficients with \(c3=a,c2=c,c4=b\). **Matches**.

49. Big rational with denominator \(P c1 + c2\). To equal GT for all \(P\), denominator must be constant: set \(c1=0\) and choose \(c2\neq 0\). Then it becomes a linear combination of \(P^{4/3},P^{1/3},P^3,P^2,P\) terms. Set coefficients of unwanted powers to 0: set \(c0=0\) (kills \(P^{4/3}\)), \(c4=0\) (kills \(P^3\)), \(c5=0,c6=0\) (kills extra \(P^2\) terms), keep \(P^{1/3}\) via \(c3/c2=a\), keep \(P^2\) via \(c? \) actually remaining \(P^2\) terms are only \(c5,c6\) so need one of them nonzero to produce \(P^2\); that’s fine—set \(c5\neq 0\) and \(c6=0\) and match \(c5/c2=c\). Keep \(P\) via \(c7,c8\) with \((c7+c8)/c2=b\). Works. **Matches**.

52. Has \(P*c5/(P+c6)\) rational; must set \(c5=0\). Remaining: \(c0P^2 + c2 P^{1+c1} + (c3+c4)P\). Need \(P^{1/3}\): set \(1+c1=1/3\Rightarrow c1=-2/3\), \(c2=a\). Then match \(c0=c\), \(c3+c4=b\). **Matches**.

53. Sine(log(exp(P^{1/3}...))) term depends on \(P\) non-algebraically; must set \(c3=0\) to remove it. Then left \(c0P^2 + (c1+c2)P\) with no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

55. Has \(t\)-rational terms; set \(c6=0,c9=0\) to remove. Remaining \(c0P^2 + c2 P^{1+c1} + (c3+c4+c5)P\). Set \(c1=-2/3\), \(c2=a\), \(c0=c\), linear sum \(=b\). **Matches**.

57. Extra \(\sin(Pc4+c5)\) depends on \(P\) non-polynomial unless \(c3=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

58. Extra \(P^{c3}c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\) depends on \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

59. Extra \(P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(Pc6+c7)\) depends on \(t\) and is non-polynomial in \(P\); set \(c4=0\). Then base form. **Matches**.

c3*(Abs(P*c4) + 1)**(c5*cos(c6*t))"]

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.991*(1 - P/39.01)*P + 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*P`

Let me expand this:
`0.991*P - 0.991*P²/39.01 + 0.991*P^(1/3) + 0.991*P`
`= 0.991*P^(1/3) - 0.02540*P² + 1.982*P`

So GT = `c_a * P^(1/3) + c_b * P² + c_c * P` where:
- c_a = 0.991
- c_b = -0.991/39.01 ≈ -0.02540
- c_c = 0.991 + 0.991 = 1.982

The GT has basis functions: **P^(1/3), P², P** — no dependence on t.

Now I'll check each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3 + P*c4*sin(c5*t + c6)`
Has P*sin(c5*t+c6) term. Set c4=0 to eliminate it. Then P^(1/3)*c0 + P²*c1 + P*(c2+c3). This matches GT.
